Book of Hawala, Chapter of Arbitration. A man claimed that a house was gifted to him at a time, so he was asked for evidence; he said: 'He denied me (the gift), so I bought it.' He provided evidence of purchase before the time he claims the gift: it is not accepted; after that time: it is accepted. And someone who said to another: 'You bought from me'... the other does not have recourse because he is a volunteer if he can be compelled (to contribute), like digging rivers, repairing a damaged ship, and ransoming a slave who committed an offense; if he cannot be compelled, he is not a volunteer, like the case of the collapse of the upper and lower floors. And if a partner spends on the animal without the permission of his partner, he does not have recourse because he could raise the matter to the judge to compel him, unlike shared crops if he spends on them without permission, for he has recourse because his partner cannot be compelled, as in al-Muhit. So he is compelled. We have already mentioned the manner of recourse, and will come, God willing, the complete issues of walls in claims and division. There is no power and no strength except with Allah, the Most High, the Great. And in the claim of a finder: a wall between two people collapsed, so one of them built it without the permission of his owner: he is a volunteer if his owner has no beams on it, nor does he. If he has beams on it, he prevents his owner from placing beams until he takes half of what he spent on the wall. End. His statement: (He claimed a house in the hand of a man, that he gifted it to him at a time, so he asked for evidence, and he said: 'He denied me, so I bought it.' He provided evidence of purchase before the time he claims the gift: it is not accepted; after it: accepted) due to the contradiction in the first case because he claims purchase after the gift and his witnesses testify to it before the gift, which is a manifest contradiction that cannot be reconciled. Their intention is contradiction between the claim and the evidence; otherwise the claimant himself has no contradiction because he did not claim purchase prior to the gift. In the second case, reconciliation is possible because the purchase occurred after the time of the gift. In his statement 'he denied me the gift' there is an indication that reconciliation is necessary. The commentator asserted that its condition is not (required) for possibility or its absence. This issue is not specific; rather in every place where contradiction occurs from the claimant, or from him and his witnesses, or from the defendant: Is possibility of reconciliation sufficient to repel it, or is actual reconciliation necessary, or is there detail? Four opinions. In al-Bazzaziyya: Shaykh al-Islam chose that possibility of reconciliation is sufficient. Bakr mentioned, and in Sharh al-Jami' al-Kabir also, that actual reconciliation is a condition in istihsan and qiyas, and sufficing with possibility. Bakr and Muhammad said: reconciliation is mentioned in some (places) and not in others, so silence is interpreted as referring to that which is mentioned. Al-Khujandi mentioned and chose that if contradiction is from the claimant, actual reconciliation is necessary and possibility is not sufficient; if from the defendant, possibility is sufficient because the apparent (truth) upon possibility is its existence, and the apparent is a proof in defense (daf') not in entitlement (istihqaq). The claimant is entitled, the defendant is... (derived from the principle of Imam al-Halwani). His statement: (like the case of collapse of the upper and lower floors) because he cannot reach his right at all and cannot benefit from his share except by repair, so he is compelled. His statement: (Four opinions) first: sufficiency of possibility absolutely, whether from claimant or defendant, whether the aspect of reconciliation is multiple or single; second: actual reconciliation is necessary, possibility not sufficient; third: what he mentioned from al-Khujandi; fourth: possibility sufficient if aspect of reconciliation is single, not if aspects are multiple. Said by some scholars. His statement: (and Bakr mentioned) etc. al-Ramli said: The answer of istihsan is the most correct, as in Munyat al-Mufti. Book of Hawala, Chapter of Arbitration. 59. Defendant, and the apparent is sufficient in defense not in entitlement. It is also said: if aspects are multiple, possibility is not sufficient; if single, possibility is sufficient. Contradiction prevents claim for oneself as it prevents claim for others. Contradiction is removed by the opponent's confirmation, by the contradictory party's retraction from the first (statement) by saying 'I abandoned it' and claiming something else, and also by the judge's falsification (takdhib), like someone who claimed that he stood surety for his debtor for a thousand, then denied the suretyship, and the creditor provided evidence that he stood surety for his debtor, and the judge ruled accordingly and took the money from the surety. Then the surety claimed against the debtor that he stood surety by his order, and provided evidence — it is accepted according to us, and he has recourse against the debtor for what he paid, because he has been legally falsified by the judgment. Similarly, if the buyer is entitled (to the property) from the buyer by judgment, he has recourse against the seller for the price, even though each buyer acknowledges the ownership of his seller, but when the judge ruled based on the evidence of the entitled party, he has become legally falsified by the inclusion of the judgment. End. Then know that they differed on the condition that both statements be before the judge. Some conditioned it; some conditioned only the second (statement) before the judge. The two opinions are mentioned in al-Bazzaziyya without preference. The second should be preferred. Among contradiction is when one claims absolutely then by a cause; if he provides evidence on the cause, (it is not accepted). His statement: (and by the retraction of the contradictory from the first) etc. Apparently from al-Bazzaziyya, but I did not see it there; what I saw there at the beginning of Kitab al-Da'wa in a section on contradiction: contradiction is removed by the opponent and by the judge's falsification. It appears that what the author mentioned about entitlement is a research from him. Then I saw al-Bazzazi mentioned later in a section on defense: the judge, if one claims by a cause and witnesses testify absolutely, it is not heard nor accepted, but his first claim is not invalidated; if he says 'I meant by the absolute the restricted,' it is heard, as previously, if he provides evidence that it is his. In al-Dhakhira also: one claimed absolutely, the defendant repelled by saying 'you previously claimed this with a restriction' and provided evidence, then the claimant says 'I now claim it by that cause and I abandon the absolute' — it is accepted and the defense is invalidated. End of what is in al-Bazzaziyya. Al-Ramli said: Perhaps what is in al-Bazzaziyya and others is problematic: one claimed against Zayd that he gave him money to give to his creditor, and made him take an oath, then claimed it against Khalid and claimed that his claim against Zayd was based on assumption — it is not accepted, because just as one right is not collected from two, one cannot litigate with two in one way. End. The aspect of its problem: when he said that his claim against Zayd was based on assumption, contradiction has been removed. And Allah knows best. Mentioned by al-Ghazzi. I say: I have written a distinction in my commentary on Jami' al-Fusulayn between the branch of al-Bazzazi and the branch he mentioned; refer to it. The distinction here is that in what al-Bazzazi mentioned, removal of contradiction is prevented because it relates to two persons, so the claim is invalid due to the impossibility of litigating with two in one right; this is absent in the case of one person, and that is the subject of this commentary. So reflect. His statement: (the second should be preferred) said in Manh al-Ghaffar after quoting: he did not mention the reason for preferring it; perhaps because it is the one by which contradiction is actualized. End. And we previously quoted from al-Nahr in the chapter of entitlement that he said: the most correct in my view is that both (statements) be before the judge, because among the conditions of a claim is that it be before him. Some scholars narrated from al-`Allama al-Maqdisi: it should suffice that one of them be before the judge; indeed, the difference is nearly verbal, because what occurred before the judge's session must be established before him for the occurrence of contradiction to be based on what he has, and what is established by evidence is like what is established by sight, so it is as if both are in the judge's session. Thus, whoever conditioned that both be in his session includes the real and the constructive.
Source pages p. 58

Commentary
This passage is a commentary from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq on Kanz al-Daqa'iq, addressing the chapter of Hawala and Arbitration. It begins with rulings on contradictory claims in court, using the example of a man who claims a house was gifted to him, then later purchased from the same owner. The key principle: if he provides evidence of purchase before the claimed gift time, it is not accepted due to apparent contradiction; if after, it is accepted because reconciliation is possible. The commentary then expands into a general discussion of contradiction in court claims, presenting four intra-Hanafi opinions on whether the mere possibility of reconciliation suffices or actual reconciliation is required. The author favors the view that possibility suffices, especially for the defendant, as apparent truth aids defense not entitlement. Examples include spending on common property without permission (where recourse depends on ability to compel via judge), wall repair, and suretyship cases where a judge's ruling legally 'falsifies' a party, removing contradiction. The passage concludes with a nuanced discussion of whether both contradictory statements must be before the judge, preferring the view that only one needs to be, as evidence establishes past statements constructively.

Key Terms
تناقض (tanāquḍ): Contradiction between two statements (claim and evidence) that makes them inconsistent on the surface.
إمكان التوفيق (imkān al-tawfīq): The possibility of reconciling two contradictory statements by interpretation, without requiring the claimant to explicitly do so.
توفيق بالفعل (tawfīq bi al-fi'l): Actual reconciliation, where the claimant explicitly explains how the two statements are consistent (e.g., 'I meant the absolute as restricted').

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the relied-upon (mufta bihi) position in the passage, what is needed to overcome a contradiction in a court statement?
A) Actual reconciliation by the party who made the contradictory statements.
B) Possibility of reconciliation, especially for the defendant.
C) The retraction of the earlier statement.
D) The agreement of both parties to the reconciliation.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, a contradiction in court does not automatically defeat a claim or defense; the possibility of reconciling the statements is sufficient, especially for the defendant, based on the principle that apparent truth is a valid proof in defense.

Retraction of Iqrar: When Rejection Nullifies the Confession
Explaining when iqrar is voided by the confirmee's rejection and exceptions

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between financial iqrar and status iqrar regarding the effect of the confirmee's rejection, and apply the rule to given scenarios.

Core Idea
Financial confession is voided by rejection; status confession is not, because it is an isqat completed by the confessor alone.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq clarifies a crucial distinction in Hanafi law: not all confessions are automatically voided when the person named rejects them. The ruling depends on the subject matter—whether it concerns property (mal) or personal status (such as slavery, divorce, or lineage). Understanding this distinction is essential for correctly handling disputes involving iqrar.

Guided Path
1
Identify the subject of the iqrar
Determine whether the confession concerns property (mal) or personal status (slavery, divorce, emancipation, lineage, clientage, marriage, endowment). This classification dictates the effect of rejection.
If the subject is ambiguous, analyze the cause or context.
2
Determine the confirmee's response
Did the confirmee explicitly reject the confession? If so, proceed to apply the rule. If the confirmee remains silent or accepts, the confession stands.
Rejection must be clear and unequivocal.
3
Apply the general rule
For financial iqrar, rejection voids the confession. For status iqrar, rejection has no effect—the confession remains valid.
The basis for the distinction: financial iqrar requires acceptance (like a contract), while status iqrar is an isqat (dropping of rights) that is completed by the confessor alone.
4
Categorize the type of rejection (for financial iqrar)
If the rejection is absolute, the confession is void. If the confirmee changes the cause (e.g., from loan to price), it is binding if no contradiction exists. If the confirmee transfers the confession to another, it requires the third party's affirmation.
These sub-rules apply only to financial iqrar.
5
Verify exceptions for status matters
For iqrar of slavery, divorce, emancipation, lineage, clientage, marriage, or endowment, rejection does not nullify the confession. The confessor's statement alone establishes the status.
These cases are explicitly listed in the text.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الحوالة باب التحكيم على آخر مالاً فقال ما كان لك علي شيء قط فبرهن المدعي على ألف وهو برهن على الضمان فاتفقا على الدين واختلفا في الجهة ،فلغت وكذا لو أقر بالقرض وهو ادعى الثمن لا يلزم زوجتك بكذا لا بل بعتني لأن السبب مقصود لتباين الحلين ولذا لم يصح الإقرار بمطلقه بخلاف المال ا هـ . ولم يذكر حكم وزنها عند الإطلاق والدعوى وفي كافي الحاكم: لو أقر درهم عدداً ثم قال أثم هي وزن خمسة أو ستة وكان الإقرار منه بالكوفة فعليه مائة درهم وزن سبعة فلا يصدق على النقصان إذا لم يبين ،موصولاً، وكذا الدنانير وإن كانوا في بلاد يتعارفون على دارهم معروفة الوزن بينهم صدق ا هـ . وفي البزازية في يده عبد فقال لرجل هو عبدك فرده المقر له ثم قال بل هو عبدي وقال المقر هو عبدي فهو لذي اليد المقر، ولو قال ذو اليد للآخر هو عبدك فقال لا بل هو عبدك ثم قال الآخر بل هو عبدي وبرهن يقبل للتناقض ا هـ . وهذا بخلاف ما في الهداية من أنه لا بد من الحجة فإنه يقتضي سماع الدعوى وهو مشكل. وقيد بالإقرار بالمال احترازاً عن الإقرار بالرق والطلاق والعتاق والنسب والولاء فإنها لا ترتد بالرد أما الثلاثة الأول ففي البزازية : قال لآخر أنا عبدك فرد المقر له ثم عاد إلى تصديقه فهو عبده ولا يبطل الإقرار بالرق بالرد كما لا يبطل بجحود المولى بخلاف الإقرار بالدين والعين حيث يبطل بالرد والطلاق والعتاق لا يبطلان بالرد لأنه إسقاط يتم بالمسقط وحده ا هـ . وأما الإقرار بالنسب وولاء العتاقة ففي شرح المجمع من الولاء : وأما الإقرار بالنكاح فلم أره الآن وحاصل مسائل رد الإقرار بالمال أنه لا يخلو إما أن مطلقاً أو يرد الجهة التي عينها المقر وحولها إلى أخرى أو يرده لنفسه ويحوله إلى غيره؛ فإن كان الأول بطل، وإن كان الثاني فإن لم يكن بينهما منافاة وجب وإلا بطل، وإن كان الثالث فإن صدقه فلان تحول إليه وإلا فلا، وإن كان بطلاق أو عتاق أو ولاء أو نكاح أو وقف أو نسب أو رق لم يرتد بالرد فيقال الإقرار يرتد برد المقر له إلا هذه في المسائل .
Book of Transfer, Chapter of Arbitration: Regarding someone who claimed against another property, and the latter said, 'You never had anything against me,' then the claimant proved a thousand, and he proved a surety, so they agreed on the debt but differed on the cause, so it is void. Similarly, if he confessed to a loan and he claimed the price, it is not binding: 'I married you for such' no, rather 'you sold me' because the cause is intended due to the difference of the two situations, and therefore a general confession is not valid, unlike property. And he did not mention the ruling of its weight at the time of absolute release and claim. In Kafi al-Hakim: If he confessed to dirhams by number, then said 'they are of weight five or six', and his confession was in Kufa, then he owes one hundred dirhams of weight seven, and he is not believed as to the deficiency if he did not clarify, connectedly. Similarly for dinars, and if they are in a land where they are accustomed to a known weight of dirhams among them, he is believed. In al-Bazzaziyyah: If a person has a slave in his hand and says to a man, 'He is your slave,' and the confirmee rejects him, then he says, 'Rather he is my slave,' and the confessor says, 'He is my slave,' then the slave belongs to the one in whose hand he is and who confessed. And if the possessor says to the other, 'He is your slave,' and he says, 'No, rather he is your slave,' then the other says, 'Rather he is my slave' and provides proof, it is accepted due to contradiction. This differs from what is in al-Hidayah that proof is necessary, for it requires hearing the claim, which is problematic. And he restricted to confession of property to exclude confession of slavery, divorce, emancipation, lineage, and clientage, for these are not nullified by rejection. As for the first three, in al-Bazzaziyyah: He said to another, 'I am your slave,' and the confirmee rejected him, then returned to affirming him, then he is his slave, and confession of slavery is not nullified by rejection just as it is not nullified by the master's denial, unlike confession of debt and chattel, which is nullified by rejection. Divorce and emancipation are not nullified by rejection because they are a dropping (isqat) that is completed by the dropper alone. As for confession of lineage and clientage of emancipation, in Sharh al-Majma' from al-Wala': As for confession of marriage, I have not seen it now. The summary of issues of rejection of confession of property is that it is either absolute, or he rejects the specified cause and changes it to another, or he rejects it for himself and transfers it to another. If the first, it is void; if the second, if there is no contradiction between them, it is binding, otherwise void; if the third, if the person affirms him, it transfers to him, otherwise not. And if it is of divorce, emancipation, clientage, marriage, endowment, lineage, or slavery, it is not nullified by rejection. So it is said that confession is nullified by the confirmee's rejection except in these cases.
Source pages p. 66

Commentary
This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq discusses the rulings on retraction of iqrar (confession) when the confirmee rejects the confession. The commentator begins by explaining that if the confirmee rejects a confession of property, the confession is void, as illustrated by the example where the defendant denies any debt but then confesses to a surety, leading to agreement on the debt but disagreement on its cause. The same applies if someone confesses to a loan while the claimant asserts it was a sale price—the confession is not binding because the cause is integral to the transaction. The passage then addresses the issue of specifying the weight of dirhams upon confession: if someone confesses to a number of dirhams without specifying weight, then later claims they were of a lighter weight, he is not believed unless the local custom defines a standard weight. Next, the commentator examines cases of contradictions in iqrar, such as when a person claims a slave belongs to someone else, then later claims the slave is his own. The ruling distinguishes between financial iqrar and iqrar involving personal status (slavery, divorce, emancipation, lineage, clientage, marriage, endowment). For financial iqrar, rejection by the confirmee nullifies the confession. For status-related iqrar, rejection has no effect because these matters involve isqat (dropping of rights), which is completed by the confessor alone. The passage summarizes that rejection of iqrar in property matters can be absolute (void), a change of cause (binding if no contradiction), or a transfer to another (requires affirmation). In contrast, iqrar of divorce, emancipation, etc., remains valid despite rejection.

Key Terms
الإقرار (al-iqrar): Confession or acknowledgment of a right or obligation
الرد (al-radd): Rejection by the confirmee of the iqrar

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) The confession is void, and the slave belongs to the confessor.

Key Takeaway
Financial iqrar is voided by the confirmee's rejection; status iqrar (slavery, divorce, emancipation, lineage, etc.) is not, because it is an isqat completed by the confessor alone.

Depositary's Acknowledgment of a Sole Heir
Ruling with proof on depositary's acknowledgment of sole heir

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the conditions under which a depositary must deliver a deposit based on his acknowledgment and distinguish between unconditional and conditional heirs.

Core Idea
A depositary's acknowledgment of a sole heir obligates delivery only if the heir is unconditional — son, daughter, father, mother.

When a depositary (the person holding a deposit) acknowledges that a certain individual is the sole heir of the deceased depositor, the question arises: must he hand over the deposit? The Hanafi school provides a detailed answer, distinguishing between heirs who inherit unconditionally (like a son) and those whose inheritance is conditional (like a brother). This lesson unpacks the ruling and its conditions from Kanz al-Daqa'iq and its commentary.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The central act is the depositary's declaration: 'This is the son of my depositor and he has no other heir.' The ruling is that the depositary must (wajib) deliver the deposit to that son.
The obligation arises from the depositary's own acknowledgment, which is binding against himself.
2
Examine the conditions for delivery
The acknowledgment must specify that the claimant is an unconditional heir (son, daughter, father, mother) and that there is no other heir. If the depositary says 'he has another heir' or is uncertain, delivery is suspended until proof is provided.
If the claimant is a brother, the judge delays because the brother's right depends on the absence of a son.
3
Distinguish unconditional vs. conditional heirs
A son inherits in all cases (unconditional), while a brother inherits only if there is no son. The immediate delivery applies only to unconditional heirs.
Daughter, father, mother are treated like the son; brother, uncle, etc. are conditional.
4
Apply the ruling to non-heir acknowledgments
If the depositary acknowledges an executor, agent, or purchaser, delivery is not made because it would infringe on the depositor's right in the specific property. However, for an agent to collect a debt, delivery is allowed.
The distinction is based on whether the right is in a specific item (deposit) or in a general obligation (debt).
5
Note the consequences of omission
If delivery is obligatory and not performed, the depositary becomes liable for compensation if the property is lost.
This reinforces the binding nature of the acknowledgment.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله: (وإن قال المودع هذا ابن مودعي لا وارث له غيره دفع المال إليه) أي وجوباً لإقراره أن ما في يده ملك الوارث خلافة عن الميت قيد بإقراره بالبنوة لأنه لو قال هذا أخوه شقيقه ولا وارث له غيره وهو يدعيه فالقاضي يتأنى في ذلك، والفرق أن استحقاق الأخ بشرط عدم الابن بخلاف الابن لأنه وارث على كل حال وتمامه مع بيان مدة التأني في فتح القدير. وقيد بقوله لا وارث له غيره لأنه لو قال له وارث غيره ولا أدري أمات للاحتراز عن الملتقط إذا أقر بها لرجل فقيه اختلاف كما ذكره الشارح، والعارية والعين المغصوبة كالوديعة. ومراده من الابن من يرث بكل حال فالبنت والأب والأم كالابن وكل من يرث في حال دون حال هو كالأخ. وفي His statement: 'And if the depositary says, "This is the son of my depositor, and he has no other heir," he gives the property to him'—i.e., it is obligatory, because his acknowledgment establishes that what is in his hand is the property of the heir, as the successor of the deceased. He restricted it to acknowledgment of being a son because if he said, 'This is his full brother and he has no other heir,' and the claimant claims it, the judge delays the decision. The difference is that the brother's entitlement is conditional on the absence of a son, while the son inherits in all cases. The complete statement with the explanation of the period of delay is in Fath al-Qadir. He restricted it with 'he has no other heir' because if he said, 'He has another heir and I do not know whether he died or not,' nothing is given to him, neither before delay nor after, until the claimant brings proof that 'we do not know of any other heir for him.' And he indicated by 'deposit' that if a debtor says, 'This is the son of my creditor,' he is ordered to give to him a fortiori. He restricted it with 'heir' to exclude the case where he acknowledges that he is his executor or agent or purchaser from him, for then he does not give it to him because it would invalidate the right of the depositor in the specific property by removing it from his possession, because the depositor's hand is like the owner's hand, so his acknowledgment against it is not accepted. But after his death it is different, unlike if he acknowledges that he is the agent of the claimant to receive his debt, where he is ordered to give to him because it is an acknowledgment of his own right, since debts are fulfilled by their equivalents. If he gives to an agent in a deposit, some say he cannot retrieve it because he would be working to nullify what he has obligated, but he should be able to retrieve it because his acknowledgment is void regarding the owner's right, and preservation is obligatory upon him, so by giving he becomes a transgressor. Therefore, he is liable if the owner denies the agency. And if he does not hand over to the agent and it is lost, some say he is not liable, but he should be liable by virtue of his own presumption. He restricted it with 'deposit' to exclude the finder (mul-taqit) who acknowledges it to someone, for there is a difference of opinion, as the commentator mentioned. The borrowed item and the usurped item are like the deposit. His intention by 'son' is one who inherits in all cases, so the daughter, father, and mother are like the son, and everyone who inherits in some cases is like the brother. In Fath al-Qadir: 'If he claims to be the brother of the absent person and that he died and he is his heir with no other heir, or claims to be his son or father or his freed slave, or if a woman claims to be his paternal aunt, maternal aunt, or brother's daughter, and says, "I have no other heir," and another claims to be the husband or wife of the deceased, or that the deceased bequeathed all or one-third of his property to him, and the possessor confirms both and says, "I do not know if the deceased has another heir or not," then the claimant of the bequest gets nothing by this acknowledgment. The judge gives to the father, mother, brother, freed slave, paternal aunt, maternal aunt, brother's daughter if alone. But when together, the claimant of son-ship does not compete with the claimant of brotherhood. However, these claimants, if opposed by the claimant of marriage or bequest of all or one-third, using the possessor's acknowledgment as evidence, the claimant of brotherhood or son-ship is preferred after the son takes an oath that this is not the deceased's wife or legatee, if there is no evidence for marriage or bequest. If evidence is given, it is taken. End of quote. And the author indicated that if the possessor acknowledges that the deceased acknowledged that this is his son, father, or freed slave, he takes it. End. And the heir blocks the brother, so he does not inherit. And the author understood that it was a condition for the woman's inheritance as well, but that is not the case apparently, so there is no contradiction. Consider. His statement: And its completion with the explanation of the period of delay is in Fath al-Qadir, where he said: 'However, it is possible that someone else participates, and that is unlikely. If he delays and another heir appears, he gives the property to him because he is the successor of the deceased. And if not...'
Source pages p. 74

Commentary
This passage is a detailed commentary on a ruling from the matn of Kanz al-Daqa'iq: If a depositary (the person holding a deposit) says, 'This person is the son of my depositor and he has no other heir,' then he must give the deposited property to that son. The commentator explains that this is obligatory because the depositary's own acknowledgment establishes that the property belongs to the heir as the successor of the deceased. The ruling is restricted to acknowledgment of being a son (or similarly a daughter, father, mother—any heir that inherits unconditionally) because if he acknowledges someone as a brother, the judge must delay the decision since the brother's right is conditional on the absence of a son, and there may be a son. The phrase 'no other heir' is a condition: if the depositary acknowledges there is another heir or is uncertain, nothing is given until the claimant provides proof that there is no other known heir. The commentary further distinguishes between acknowledging an heir (like a son) and acknowledging a non-heir (like an executor or agent). The latter does not warrant delivery because it would infringe on the depositor's right to the specific property. However, if the depositary acknowledges an agent to receive a debt, delivery is made because debts are not specific items. The text then discusses nuances: if the agency is not proven, the depositary may be liable. It also addresses that the same applies to a borrowed item or usurped item. The latter part of the passage from Fath al-Qadir elaborates on multiple claimants and the priority among them. The overall ruling is that the depositary is bound to deliver to a clear heir based on his own acknowledgment, but with careful restrictions to protect the rights of the depositor and other possible heirs.

Key Terms
المودع (al-mudi'): In this passage, it refers to the depositary (the person who holds the deposit), as he is the one who acknowledges the heir.
الوديعة (al-wadi'ah): Deposit; property entrusted to someone for safekeeping without compensation.
الوارث (al-warith): Heir; one entitled to inherit from the deceased.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Why must the judge delay delivery if the depositary acknowledges a brother as heir?
A) Because the brother is a conditional heir, and a son might exist
B) Because the brother must produce witnesses
C) Because the depositary's acknowledgment is not valid for brothers
D) Because the judge must verify the brother's identity

Key Takeaway
A depositary must deliver a deposit to an acknowledged sole heir only if the heir is unconditional (son, daughter, father, mother) and the acknowledgment includes the phrase 'no other heir'.

Depositary's Acknowledgment of a Second Claimant
Commentary on a depositary's conflicting acknowledgments

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling when a depositary acknowledges a second claimant after a first valid acknowledgment, and identify the condition under which the depositary becomes liable to the second.

Core Idea
A later acknowledgment against a prior valid claim is ineffective unless the prior confirms; depositary may be liable for breach.

In this passage, Ibn Nujaym comments on a ruling from al-Kanz concerning a depositary who first acknowledges one person as the depositor's son, then later acknowledges another. The first son denies the second. The property is given to the first, but the commentators disagree on whether the depositary must compensate the second. This lesson unpacks the ruling and the dispute, which hinges on the nature of the second acknowledgment as 'iqrar 'ala al-ghair (acknowledgment against a third party).

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and the ruling
The depositary first acknowledges A as the son of the depositor, then later acknowledges B as also a son. The first son denies. The ruling: property is judged for the first.
The first acknowledgment is valid because no one denies it.
2
Understand why the second acknowledgment is ineffective
The second acknowledgment is 'iqrar 'ala al-ghair (acknowledgment against a third party) because it affects the first son's right. It is not binding on the first without his confirmation.
This is a fundamental Hanafi principle in acknowledgments.
3
Recognize the dispute on depositary's liability
The author of al-Kanz did not mention liability because of ikhtilaf. Ghayat al-Bayan: no liability (sonship does not prove ownership). Al-Binaya: liability if property was given to the first without a judge's order, analogizing to a dismissed qadi case. Fath al-Qadir prefers liability.
The mufta bihi is liability per Fath al-Qadir.
4
Apply the condition for liability
The depositary is liable to the second only if he gave the property to the first without a judicial order. If he withheld or acted under court order, no liability.
This condition reconciles the conflicting views.
5
Extend to analogous cases
The same principle applies to acknowledgments of deposit, usurpation, loan, or debt: the first is preferred, and the bailee/possessor is liable to the second if he acted without a judge's order.
The source provides several examples at the end.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (وإن قال لآخر هذا ابنه أيضاً وكذبه الأول قضى للأول) أي قال المودع هذا ابنه بعد إقراره للأول بأنه ابنه وكذبه المقر له قضى بالمال للمقر له الأول لأن الثاني إقرار على الغير لصحة الإقرار للأول لعدم من يكذبه. ولم يذكر المصنف ضمان المودع للثاني لاختلاف الشارحين فيه ففي غاية البيان أنه لا يغرم المودع للابن الثاني شيئاً بإقراره له لأن استحقاقه لم يثبت فلم يتحقق التلف وهذا لأنه لا يلزم من مجرد ثبوت البنوة ثبوت الإرث فلا يكون الإقرار بالبنوة إقراراً بالمال ا.هـ. وفي البناية: فإن قيل ينبغي أن يضمن المودع هنا للمقر له الثاني كما قلنا في مودع القاضي المعزول إذا بدأ بالإقرار بما في يده لإنسان ثم أقر بأن القاضي المعزول سلمه فإنه يضمن للقاضي على ما مر من قبل قلنا : هذا أيضاً يضمن نصيبه إذا دفع إلى المقر له الأول بغير قضاء القاضي ا هـ. وهذا هو الصواب كما في فتح القدير. وقيد بإقراره بالولد لأنه لو أقر المودع بها لرجل ثم قال لا بل وديعة فلان أو قال غصبت هذا من فلان لا بل من فلان وكذا العارية فإنه يقضى به للأول ويضمن للثاني قيمته، وكذا في الإقرار بالدين، فلو قال هذا لفلان إلا نصفه فلفلان فكما قال، ولو قال هذان لفلان إلا هذا فلفلان كان مصدقاً، فلو قال هذا لفلان وهذا لفلان المقر له إلا الأول فإنه لي لم يصدق وهما للأول، ولو قال هذا لفلان وهذا لفلان المقر له إلا نصفه الأول فإنه لفلان كان جائزاً، ولو قال هذه الحنطة والشعير لفلان إلا كراً من هذه الحنطة إذا كانت الحنطة أكثر من الكر؛ كذا في الأصل لمولانا محمد من الدعوى.
His statement: (And if he says to another: This is also his son, and the first denies, he is judged in favor of the first) i.e., the depositary said: This is his son, after acknowledging to the first that he is his son, and the acknowledged one denied the second, then the property is judged for the first acknowledged one because the second is an acknowledgment against another (igrar 'ala al-ghair), and the first acknowledgment is valid because there is no one to deny it. And the author did not mention the liability (daman) of the depositary to the second due to difference among commentators. In Ghayat al-Bayan: he is not liable to the second son for anything by his acknowledgment because his entitlement is not established, so loss is not realized, and because mere proof of sonship does not entail proof of inheritance, so acknowledgment of sonship is not acknowledgment of property. End. In al-Binaya: if it is said that the depositary should be liable to the second here as we said in the case of the depositary of the dismissed qadi when he first acknowledges to someone what is in his hand, then acknowledges that the dismissed qadi gave it to him, he is liable to the qadi as previously, we say: here too he is liable for his share if he gave it to the first without a judge's order. End. And this is the correct view as in Fath al-Qadir. And it is restricted to his acknowledgment of a child because if the depositary acknowledged to a man then said: no rather it is the deposit of so-and-so, or said: I usurped this from so-and-so, no rather from so-and-so, similarly for a loan (ariyah), judgment is for the first and he is liable to the second for its value, and similarly in acknowledgment of debt. If he said: this is for so-and-so except half of it, then it is for so-and-so as he said. If he said: these two are for so-and-so except this one, then it is for so-and-so, he is believed. If he said: this is for so-and-so and this is for so-and-so the acknowledged one except the first is mine, he is not believed and both are for the first. If he said: this is for so-and-so and this is for so-and-so the acknowledged one except half of the first, then it is for so-and-so, it is permissible. If he said: this wheat and barley are for so-and-so except a kurr from this wheat if the wheat is more than a kurr; so in al-Asl by our master Muhammad on claims.
Source pages p. 75

Commentary
Passage type: Ruling with proof (commentary). This passage addresses the scenario where the depositary first acknowledges one person as the son of the depositor, then later says to a second person 'this is also his son,' and the first denies the second's claim. The ruling is that the property is given to the first acknowledged son because the second acknowledgment is against someone else (إقرار على الغير) and the first acknowledgment is valid as there is no one to deny it. The author (صاحب الكنز) did not mention whether the depositary is liable (ضمان) to the second son due to disagreement among commentators. The text presents two views: (1) In Ghayat al-Bayan, no liability because the second's entitlement is not proven; (2) In al-Binaya, liability if the depositary gave the property to the first without a judge's order, analogizing to the case of the depositary of a dismissed qadi. The correct view per Fath al-Qadir is that the depositary is liable for the second's share if he gave to the first without judicial order. Then the passage provides additional distinctions: if the depositary makes contradictory acknowledgments regarding deposit, usurpation, loan, or debt, the first is preferred and he is liable to the second. Several examples illustrate the rules of partial acknowledgments and exceptions.

Key Terms
إقرار على الغير (iqrar 'ala al-ghair): An acknowledgment that affects another's right; not fully binding without the other's confirmation.
الضمان (al-daman): Liability to compensate for loss; here, the depositary may be liable to the second claimant if he gave the property to the first improperly.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the correct view (as in Fath al-Qadir), under what condition does the depositary become liable to the second son?
A) He is always liable.
B) He is liable only if the first son denies the second.
C) He is liable if he gave the property to the first without a judge's order.
D) He is never liable.

Key Takeaway
The first acknowledgment takes precedence; the depositary's liability for a second acknowledgment arises only if he acted without judicial order.

Depositary's Acknowledgment of Multiple Heirs and Partial Acknowledgments
Ruling on depositary's acknowledgment of multiple sons and partial acknowledgments

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi rules of acknowledgment (iqrar) to scenarios involving a depositary's conflicting claims, including the requirement of judicial order for liability.

Core Idea
An acknowledgment that contradicts a prior valid one is void, but liability arises if the depositary pays without a judge's order.

In trust law, a depositary (mudi') holds property on behalf of another. When he acknowledges multiple claimants, priority goes to the first uncontested acknowledgment. However, if he pays out without a judge's ruling, he may be liable to the second claimant. This passage from Al-Bahr al-Raiq explores this principle and extends it to various partial acknowledgments, demonstrating the meticulous application of iqrar in Hanafi fiqh.

Guided Path
1
State the base ruling
Identify that when the depositary acknowledges two sons and the first denies the second, judgment is for the first son because the second is an acknowledgment against a third party.
The first acknowledgment is valid due to lack of a denier.
2
Identify the ikhtilaf on liability
Compare the view of Ghayat al-Bayan (no liability because paternity does not entail inheritance) with al-Binayah (liability if paid without judge's order). Note that Fath al-Qadir declares the latter correct.
This is an intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf.
3
Trace the qiyas
Understand the analogous case of the depositary of a dismissed judge: if he acknowledges a person and then acknowledges the judge gave it to him, he is liable to the judge. Similarly, here liability arises from payment without judicial order.
The illa is the act of paying without a judge's order when there is a conflicting claim.
4
Apply to other scenarios
The same principle applies when the depositary initially acknowledges a property as a deposit, usurpation, or loan, then changes his statement: judgment for the first, and he is liable for the value to the second if he paid without judicial order.
The ruling is consistent across various claims.
5
Analyze partial acknowledgment examples
Examine the examples of exceptions (e.g., 'this is for X except half', 'these two are for X except this one'). Understand the logic: the depositary is believed in his statements except when they are contradictory or self-serving.
These examples illustrate the application of iqrar rules to complex claims.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (وإن قال لآخر هذا ابنه أيضاً وكذبه الأول قضى للأول) أي قال المودع هذا ابنه بعد إقراره للأول بأنه ابنه وكذبه المقر له قضى بالمال للمقر له الأول لأن الثاني إقرار على الغير لصحة الإقرار للأول لعدم من يكذبه. ولم يذكر المصنف ضمان المودع للثاني لاختلاف الشارحين فيه ففي غاية البيان أنه لا يغرم المودع للابن الثاني شيئاً بإقراره له لأن استحقاقه لم يثبت فلم يتحقق التلف وهذا لأنه لا يلزم من مجرد ثبوت البنوة ثبوت الإرث فلا يكون الإقرار بالبنوة إقراراً بالمال ا.هـ. وفي البناية: فإن قيل ينبغي أن يضمن المودع هنا للمقر له الثاني كما قلنا في مودع القاضي المعزول إذا بدأ بالإقرار بما في يده لإنسان ثم أقر بأن القاضي المعزول سلمه فإنه يضمن للقاضي على ما مر من قبل قلنا : هذا أيضاً يضمن نصيبه إذا دفع إلى المقر له الأول بغير قضاء القاضي ا هـ. وهذا هو الصواب كما في فتح القدير. وقيد بإقراره بالولد لأنه لو أقر المودع بها لرجل ثم قال لا بل وديعة فلان أو قال غصبت هذا من فلان لا بل من فلان وكذا العارية فإنه يقضى به للأول ويضمن للثاني قيمته، وكذا في الإقرار بالدين، فلو قال هذا لفلان إلا نصفه فلفلان فكما قال، ولو قال هذان لفلان إلا هذا فلفلان كان مصدقاً، فلو قال هذا لفلان وهذا لفلان المقر له إلا الأول فإنه لي لم يصدق وهما للأول، ولو قال هذا لفلان وهذا لفلان المقر له إلا نصفه الأول فإنه لفلان كان جائزاً، ولو قال هذه الحنطة والشعير لفلان إلا كراً من هذه الحنطة إذا كانت الحنطة أكثر من الكر؛ كذا في الأصل لمولانا محمد من الدعوى.
His statement: 'And if he says to another: This is his son as well, and the first denies him, judgment is given for the first.' That is, the depositary says: This is his son after he had acknowledged the first as his son, and the first denies the second, then judgment is given for the first with the property, because the second is an acknowledgment against a third party, since the acknowledgment for the first is valid due to the absence of anyone to deny him. And the author did not mention the liability of the depositary to the second due to the difference among the commentators. In Ghayat al-Bayan: The depositary is not liable to the second son for anything by his acknowledgment, because his entitlement has not been established, so loss has not occurred. This is because mere establishment of paternity does not entail establishment of inheritance; thus acknowledgment of paternity is not acknowledgment of property. In al-Binayah: If it is said that the depositary should be liable here to the second as we said in the case of the depositary of a dismissed judge, if he begins by acknowledging what is in his hand to a person, then acknowledges that the dismissed judge had given it to him, he is liable to the judge as previously mentioned. We say: This one is also liable for his share if he gives it to the first without a judge's ruling. This is correct as in Fath al-Qadir. And it is restricted to his acknowledgment of a child, because if the depositary acknowledged for a man, then said: 'No, rather it is a deposit of so-and-so' or said: 'I usurped this from so-and-so, no rather from so-and-so,' and likewise in 'ariyah (loan), then judgment is given for the first and he is liable to the second for its value. Likewise in acknowledgment of debt. If he says: 'This is for so-and-so except half, then it is for so-and-so,' then it is as he says. If he says: 'These two are for so-and-so except this one, then it is for so-and-so,' he is believed. If he says: 'This is for so-and-so and this is for so-and-so except the first, then it is mine,' he is not believed, and both are for the first. If he says: 'This is for so-and-so and this is for so-and-so except half of the first, then it is for so-and-so,' it is permissible. If he says: 'This wheat and barley is for so-and-so except a kurr of this wheat, if the wheat is more than the kurr,' — as in al-Asl of our master Muhammad from the chapter of claims.
Source pages p. 76

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on a line from Kanz al-Daqa'iq about a depositary (mudi') who initially acknowledges a property as belonging to a person who claims to be the son of the deceased, then later acknowledges another person as also a son. The first son denies the second. The ruling is that judgment is given for the first son, because the second acknowledgment is effectively an acknowledgment against a third party (the first son) and cannot override the first valid acknowledgment. The key issue is whether the depositary is liable to the second son for the property. The commentators differ: according to Ghayat al-Bayan, he is not liable because paternity does not automatically establish inheritance, so the acknowledgment of paternity is not an acknowledgment of property rights. However, in al-Binayah, it is argued that the depositary would be liable if he gave the property to the first son without a judge's order, similar to the case of the depositary of a dismissed judge. This is considered the correct view in Fath al-Qadir. The passage then provides various scenarios of partial acknowledgments and exceptions, illustrating the detailed rules of iqrar in Hanafi law. Each scenario demonstrates the principle that the confessant is believed regarding what he says, except when it involves an acknowledgment against a third party or a contradiction that is inherently self-serving. These examples come from al-Asl by Imam Muhammad.

Key Terms
مودع (mudi'): A depositary, someone who holds property in trust (wadi'ah).
إقرار (iqrar): An acknowledgment or confession that something belongs to another, which creates legal consequences.
إقرار بالبنوة (iqrar bi al-bunuwwa): Acknowledgment of paternity, i.e., declaring someone as one's son.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the preferred view in this passage, when is a depositary liable to a second acknowledged son?
A) Always, because he acknowledged him.
B) Only if he gave the property to the first son without a judge's ruling.
C) Only if the judge orders him to pay.
D) He is never liable because paternity does not establish inheritance.

Key Takeaway
A depositary must not distribute property to a claimant if there is a conflicting claim without a judge's order, lest he becomes personally liable.

Present Heir Representing Absent Co-Heirs
Explains the ruling that a present heir can represent absent co-heirs when the entire property is in his hand.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the condition for a present heir to represent absent co-heirs in a claim of specific property and distinguish between the rulings for 'ayn and dayn.

Core Idea
A present heir can represent absent co-heirs only if the entire property is in his hand.

This passage from the Hanafi fiqh tradition addresses a practical scenario in estate claims: when some heirs are present and others absent, can the present heir act as a representative for the absent ones in court? The ruling establishes a crucial condition—the entire property must be in the present heir's possession. We will also explore the distinction between claims over specific property (ayn) and debts (dayn) and the differing views within the Hanafi school regarding movable property.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Condition for Representation
Find the condition that the text sets for a present heir to represent absent co-heirs in a property claim. The text says 'it is necessary for all of it to be in his hand' (yajibu an takun kulluha fi yadihi).
This condition appears in al-Jami' al-Kabir and is the majority view.
2
Distinguish Between 'Ayn and Dayn
Note the disagreement: according to the apparent meaning of al-Hidayah, al-Nihayah, and al-'Inayah, the same condition applies even in debt claims. However, Fath al-Qadir distinguishes between specific property ('ayn) and debt (dayn), which the text declares as the correct view.
The text says 'and that is the truth; other than that is an oversight.'
3
Understand the Two Indications from 'He Takes Only Half'
The phrase 'he takes only half of what is claimed' implies (i) no guarantor is taken from the possessor, and (ii) the present heir takes an undivided (musha') half share.
The half is undivided because the property is not partitioned at this stage.
4
Analyze the Ruling on Movable vs. Immovable Property
The ruling is restricted to immovable property (aqar). For movable property, it is placed with a trustworthy person until the owner appears. Note the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf: Abu Hanifa holds that movable property is not taken from the possessor, while Abu Yusuf and Muhammad hold that it is taken and entrusted.
The text says 'on the two's view' (qawluhuma) refers to Abu Yusuf and Muhammad.
5
Recognize the Exception When the Possessor Admits
If the possessor admits the claim (is muqirran), it is not taken from him. This is agreed upon by all.
See Jami' al-Fusulayn.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الكل، وإن كان البعض في يده نفذ بقدره كما صرح به في الجامع الكبير. وظاهر ما في الهداية والنهاية والعناية أنه لا بد من كونها كلها في يده في دعوى الدين أيضاً. وصرح في فتح القدير بالفرق بين العين والدين وهو الحق وغيره سهو. وفي قوله «أخذ نصف المدعى فقط إشارتان: الأولى أنه لا يؤخذ من ذي اليد كفيل لأن القاضي نصب لقطع الخصومات لا لإنشائها. الثانية أن الحاضر يأخذ النصف مشاعاً غير مقسوم كما صرح به العمادي في الفصول. وقيد بالعقار لأن المنقول يوضع عند عدل إلى حضور صاحبه. وقيل هو كالعقار لا يؤخذ منه ولا شك أنه على قولهما يؤخذ منه ويوضع على يد عدل، وأجمعوا على أنه لا يؤخذ لو مقراً؛ كذا في جامع الفصولين.
All of it, and if some of it is in his hand, it is effective to the extent of what is in his hand, as stated in al-Jami' al-Kabir. And the apparent meaning in al-Hidayah, al-Nihayah, and al-'Inayah is that it is necessary for all of it to be in his hand even in a claim of debt. And it is stated in Fath al-Qadir that there is a difference between a specific property and a debt, and that is the truth; other than that is an oversight. And in his statement 'he takes only half of what is claimed' there are two indications: first, that a guarantor is not taken from the possessor because the judge is appointed to end disputes, not to initiate them. Second, that the present person takes an undivided half, as stated by al-'Imadi in al-Fusul. And it is restricted to immovable property because movable property is placed with a trustworthy person until its owner appears. And it is said that it is like immovable property and is not taken from him; and there is no doubt that according to the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) it is taken from him and placed with a trustworthy person, and they all agreed that it is not taken if he admits; as in Jami' al-Fusulayn.
Source pages p. 78

Commentary
This passage is a ruling statement from the chapter on arbitration (tahkim) in the Hanafi madhhab. It discusses the condition for a present heir to represent absent co-heirs in a property claim. The rule is that if the entire property is in the hand of the present heir, he can be a representative for the absent heirs even in a debt claim (according to the majority view). However, Fath al-Qadir distinguishes between a specific property (ayn) and a debt (dayn), which is the correct view. The phrase 'he takes only half' indicates that the present heir does not take a guarantor from the possessor, and he takes an undivided half share. The ruling applies to immovable property; movable property is entrusted to a neutral person. According to Abu Yusuf and Muhammad, movable property is also taken and entrusted. If the possessor admits the claim, it is not taken.

Key Terms
العين (al-'ayn): Specific, tangible property (immovable or movable) that is the subject of a claim.
الدين (al-dayn): A debt owed by the deceased or estate, not a specific item.
مشاع (musha'): Undivided share; the present heir takes an undivided half of the property claimed.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the text, what is the condition for a present heir to represent absent co-heirs in a claim of specific property ('ayn)?
A) The present heir must have the property in his hand, even if only partially.
B) The entire property must be in the present heir's hand.
C) The absent heirs must all be minors.
D) The property must be movable.

Key Takeaway
A present heir can represent absent co-heirs only if the entire property is in his possession; movable property is treated differently and entrusted to a neutral person.

Ruling on Modification by the Defendant
Ruling with rational proof on defendant's ta'dil.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on a defendant's ta'dil of witnesses and distinguish the valid exception of admission from mere attestation.

Core Idea
A defendant's attestation of a witness's reliability is invalid unless it amounts to an admission of the claim.

In Hanafi court procedure, the defendant is the adversary of the plaintiff and his witnesses. Therefore, any statement by the defendant that merely confirms the witnesses' uprightness is considered suspect and is not accepted as valid ta'dil. However, if the defendant's words indicate an admission of the right being claimed, that statement is binding. This lesson unpacks the reasoning behind this rule and its practical implications.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is the defendant's statement declaring the plaintiff's witnesses to be upright ('adl). The ruling is that this ta'dil is not accepted (la yasihh) in court.
The defendant's adversarial position is the key reason for invalidity.
2
Locate the dalil (proof)
The proof is aqli (rational): since the defendant denies the claim, his praise of the plaintiff's witnesses is inherently contradictory and unreliable.
No specific textual evidence is cited; it is based on legal logic (istihsan or ma'qul).
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The defendant's position of opposition (khismah) to the plaintiff means his statement about the witnesses is not trustworthy. The witness's own testimony is more credible than the defendant's opinion of the witness.
The exception arises when the defendant's words admit the claim, making him no longer an adversary.
4
Note the exception
If the defendant says 'they told the truth' or 'they are upright and truthful', this is an admission of the right and thus valid, because he is no longer denying.
The phrase 'they are upright' alone, without admission, is insufficient.
5
Consider the intra-Hanafi dispute
A separate issue is whether one witness can modify his fellow witness. The passage indicates a difference of opinion: some Hanafi scholars accept it, others do not.
This dispute is within the Hanafi school and affects how the judge handles witness credibility.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
جرح الشاهد نفسه ولو خرسا أو عميا لا يقضى. تاب الفاسق لا يعدل كما تاب بل لا بد من مضي زمان يقع في القلب صدقه في التوبة ا هـ. تنبیه آخر ولو زكى من في السر علناً يجوز عندنا، والخصاف شرط تغايرهما ؛ كذا في البزازية. وفي المصباح علن الأمر علونا من باب قعد ظهر وانتشر فهو عالن وعلن علناً من باب تعب لغة فهو علن وعلين والاسم العلانية مخففاً ا هـ. تنبيه آخر : يسأل القاضي عن الشهود الذمة عدول المسلمين وإلا فيسأل عنهم عدول الكفار؛ كذا في المحيط والاختيار قوله : ( وتعديل الخصم لا يصح) أي تزكية المدعى عليه الشاهد بقوله هو عدل غير مقبولة لأن في زعم المدعي وشهوده أن الخصم كاذب في إنكاره مبطل في إصراره فلا يصلح معدلاً، وموضوع المسألة إذا قال عدول إلا أنهم أخطؤوا أو نسوا، أما إذا قال صدقوا أو هم عدول صدقة فقد اعترف بالحق؛ كذا في الهداية. وفي شرح أدب القضاء للصدر الشهيد أن يكون مقراً بقوله صدقوا فيما شهدوا به علي وبقوله هم عدول فيما شهدوا به علي أطلقه وقيده في البزازية بما إذا كان المدعى عليه لا يرجع إليه في التعديل فإن كان صح قوله وشمل الخصم المدعي والمدعى عليه وإن أراد به المدعى عليه وهو الظاهر فعدم صحته من المدعي بأولى كتعديل الشاهد نفسه. وأما فمقبول لما في البزازية : وقول الشاهد إنه ليس بعدل إقراره على نفسه جائز عليه وكان ينبغي له أن لا يفعل ا هـ. وظاهر ما في الظهيرية أنه يأثم بذلك حيث كان صادقاً . في شهادته لما فيه من إبطال حق المدعي. ولم يذكر المؤلف رحمه الله تعديل أحد الشاهدين صاحبه وفيه اختلاف ؛ قال في الظهيرية : شاهدان شهدا لرجل والقاضي يعرف أحدهما بالعدالة ولا يعرف الآخر فعدله الذي عرفه القاضي بالعدالة . قال نصير رحمه الله : لا يقبل القاضي تعديله ولابن سلمة فيه قولان، وعن أبي بكر البلخي في ثلاثة شهدوا والقاضي يعرف اثنين منهم بالعدالة ولا يعرف الثالث فإن القاضي يقبل تعديلهما لو شهد هذا الثالث شهادة أخرى ولا يقبل تعديلهما في الشهادة الأولى وهو كما قال نصير رحمه الله تعالى ا هـ . وأطلقه فشمل ما إذا عدله المدعى عليه قبل الشهادة أو بعدها كما في البزازية ويحتاج إلى تأمل فإنه قبل الدعوى لم يوجد منه كذب في إنكاره وقت التعديل وكان الفسق الطارئ على المعدل قبل القضاء كالمقارن. وفي البزازية : ولا يسأل رجلاً له على المشهود عليه دين فلسه الحاكم، وهذا دليل على أن الشاهد إذا كان له دين على المشهود عليه وهو مفلس لا تقبل اهـ. وفي المحيط البرهاني من دفع الدعاوى معزياً إلى الأوزجندي : إذا قال المدعى عليه بعد الشهادة لي دفع لا يكون تعديلاً للشهود الجواز أن يكون بالطعن في الشاهد ا هـ . قلت : بخلاف قول المدعي عليه في جواب دعوى الوكيل بالدين دفعته إلى الموكل أو أبرأني فإنه يكون إقراراً بالوكالة فإنه يؤمر بالدفع إلى الوكيل كما سيأتي فيها .
Disqualification of the witness himself: Even if deaf or blind, his testimony is not accepted. The sinful person who repents is not considered trustworthy at the moment of repentance; rather, time must pass such that his truthfulness in repentance becomes firmly settled in the heart. End. Another note: If one gives secret tazkiya publicly, it is permissible according to us, but al-Khassaf requires them to be different; as in al-Bazzaziyya. In al-Misbah: Alana al-amr from the root qa'ada zahara wa-intashara, so it is 'alin, and alina from the root ta'iba is also a language, so it is 'aln and 'alayyin, and the noun is al-alaniyya with tashdid. End. Another note: The judge asks about witnesses: if they are dhimmis, he asks upright Muslims; otherwise he asks upright non-Muslims; as in al-Muhit and al-Ikhtiyar. His saying: 'And the modification by the defendant is not valid' means the attestation of the defendant of the witness by saying 'he is upright' is not accepted because according to the plaintiff and his witnesses, the defendant is lying in his denial and wrong in his insistence, so he is not fit to be a modifier. The subject of the issue is when he says 'they are upright but they erred or forgot'; but if he says 'they told the truth' or 'they are upright and truthful', then he has admitted the right; as in al-Hidayah. In Sharh Adab al-Qada of al-Sadr al-Shahid: that he confesses by his statement 'they told the truth in what they testified against me' and by his statement 'they are upright in what they testified against me' - he made it absolute and restricted it in al-Bazzaziyya to when the defendant is not relied upon for modification; if he is, his statement is valid. This includes the plaintiff and defendant, but if intended for the defendant, which is apparent, then its invalidity from the plaintiff is more likely, like the witness's own modification. As for that it is accepted, because in al-Bazzaziyya: the statement of the witness that he is not upright is his admission against himself, binding upon him, though he should not do it. End. The apparent from al-Zahiriyya is that he sins by that if he is truthful in his testimony because it invalidates the right of the plaintiff. And the author (may Allah have mercy on him) did not mention the modification of one witness by his companion, concerning which there is disagreement. It is said in al-Zahiriyya: Two witnesses testified for a man, and the judge knows one of them to be upright but not the other, so the one known to be upright modified him. Nasir (may Allah have mercy on him) said: The judge does not accept his modification, and for Ibn Salama there are two opinions. And from Abu Bakr al-Balkhi: If three testified, and the judge knows two of them to be upright but not the third, then the judge accepts their modification if this third testifies in another testimony, but does not accept their modification in the first testimony. That is as Nasir said. End. He made it absolute, so it includes whether the defendant modified him before the testimony or after, as in al-Bazzaziyya. It requires consideration: for before the claim, there is no lie from him in his denial at the time of modification, and the transgression that occurs on the modifier before the ruling is like that which accompanies it. In al-Bazzaziyya: And he does not ask a man who has a debt against the testified-against and who is insolvent, the judge makes him insolvent. This indicates that if the witness has a debt against the testified-against and he is insolvent, his testimony is not accepted. In al-Muhit al-Burhani of Daf' al-Da'awa attributed to al-Uzjandi: If the defendant says after testimony 'I have a defense', it is not a modification of the witnesses, for it may be a challenge to the witness. End. I say: Unlike the defendant's statement in response to the claim of the agent for a debt, 'I paid it to the principal' or 'he discharged me', it is an admission of agency, for he is ordered to pay to the agent, as will come later.
Source pages p. 112

Commentary
This passage is a detailed ruling on when a defendant's attestation of witnesses is acceptable. The author states that the defendant's statement 'he is upright' is generally not valid because the defendant is in a position of denying the claim, so his word is suspect. However, there is an exception: if the defendant says 'they told the truth' or 'they are upright and truthful', that constitutes an admission of the right, so it is accepted. The passage also covers various sub-issues: the judge's inquiry about witnesses from appropriate communities, and the modification of one witness by another. This is a Hanafi ruling without clear intra-school dispute here.

Key Terms
تعديل (ta'dil): Modification or attestation that a witness is upright ('adl) and reliable.
تزكية (tazkiya): Vouching for a witness's integrity; often used interchangeably with ta'dil.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
When is a defendant's statement about plaintiff's witnesses considered a valid admission (iqrar) rather than invalid ta'dil?
A) When he says 'they are upright'.
B) When he says 'they are liars'.
C) When he says 'they told the truth' or 'they are upright and truthful'.
D) When he remains silent.

Key Takeaway
A defendant's ta'dil of witnesses is generally invalid due to his adversarial position, but a statement that admits the claim is binding as an iqrar.

The Sufficiency of One Person for Tazkiya, Message, and Translation
Ruling on the number of persons for tazkiya, message, and translation with an intra-Hanafi dispute

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on the number of persons required for tazkiya, message, and translation, and explain the reasoning of Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf versus Muhammad al-Shaybani.

Core Idea
In secret tazkiya, one suffices because it is not testimony—the requirement of two is devotional and not transferable.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq addresses an important procedural question in Hanafi judicial practice: how many persons are needed to vouch for a witness's integrity (tazkiya), convey a message between judge and modifier, or translate testimony? Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf hold that one person suffices, while Muhammad al-Shaybani requires two, drawing an analogy to testimony. The passage also distinguishes secret tazkiya (where one is enough) from public tazkiya (which demands all testimonial conditions except wording). Understanding this dispute helps you grasp the Hanafi school's internal methodology and its practical impact on court proceedings.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Legal Issue
Recognize that the core question is about the required number of persons for three distinct judicial actions: tazkiya (vouching for witness integrity), risalah (conveying a message), and tarjamah (translation).
2
State the Two Hanafi Positions
Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf (the two) rule that one person suffices for all three. Muhammad al-Shaybani requires two, treating them as akin to testimony.
Intra-madhhab disagreement: all belong to the Hanafi school.
3
Analyze the Analogical Reasoning (Qiyas)
Muhammad argues by qiyas: tazkiya, message, and translation all serve to inform the judge, just like testimony, so they should have the same number requirement. The two reject this because the formalities (wording, court presence) are absent and the number rule in testimony is taa'abbudi (devotional).
Argument type: qiyas khafi (hidden analogy).
4
Identify the Practical Difference (Thamarah al-Khilaf)
If the litigant objects, the two still accept one modifier; Muhammad would reject. If the litigant consents, all agree one suffices.
5
Determine the Relied-upon Position (Mufta Bihi)
The text and later Hanafi authorities uphold the view of the two, but caution recommends two persons.
Epistemological weight: zahir al-riwayah.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (والواحد يكفي للتزكية والرسالة والترجمة وهذا عندهما. وقال محمد: لا يجوز إلا اثنان لأنهما في معنى الشهادة لأن ولاية القاضي تنبني على ظهور العدالة وهو بالتزكية فيشترط فيه العدد كالعدالة، وتشترط الذكورة في المزكي في الحدود، ولهما أنه ليس في معنى الشهادة ولهذا لا يشترط فيه لفظ الشهادة ومجلس القضاء واشتراط العدد في الشهادة أمر تحكمي أي تعبدي في الشهادة فلا يتعداها ومحل الاختلاف ما إذا لم يرض الخصم بتزكية واحد فإن رضي الخصم بتزكية واحد فزكى جاز إجماعاً ؛ كذا في الولوالجية. وأطلق في التزكية والمراد تزكية السر، ولو قال الواحد العدل المسلم لكان أولى لاشتراط العدالة فيها والإسلام في المزكي لو المشهود عليه مسلماً كما في البزازية وأطلق في الواحد فشمل العبد والمرأة والأعمى والمحدود في القذف إذا تاب والصبي وأحد الزوجين للآخر، والوالد لولده وعكسه، والعبد لمولاه وعكسه وخرج من كلامه تزكية الشاهد يشترط لها جميع ما يشترط في الشهادة من الحرية والبصر وغير ذلك إلا لفظ الشهادة إجماعاً لأن معنى الشهادة فيها أظهر فإنها تختص بمجلس القضاء، وكذا يشترط العدد فيها على ما قاله الخصاف وأطلق في الرسالة فشمل رسول القاضي إلى المزكي ورسول المزكي إلى القاضي كما في فتح القدير لا الأوّل كما زعمه الشارح وأطلق في الترجمة فشمل المترجم عن الشهود أو عن المدعي أو المدعى عليه لا الأول كما توهمه الشارح قالوا: والأحوط في الكل اثنان. وفي البزازية : ولا يعلمه أنه يسأل عنه وعلله الصدر الشهيد بأنه إذا أعلمه ربما خدع المزكي أو أخافه ولا يعلمه أنه سأل عنه سراً إنما يطلب منه تزكية العلانية، وينبغي للقاضي أن يختار في المسألة عن الشهود من هو أخبر بأحوال الناس وأكثرهم اختلاطاً بالناس مع عدالته عارفاً بما لا يكون جرحاً وما يكون جرحاً غير طماع ولا فقير كي لا يخدع بالمال فإن لم يكن في جيرانه ولا أهل سوقه من يثق به سأل أهل محلته وإن لم يجد فيهم ثقة اعتبر فيهم تواتر الأخبار ؛ كذا ذكره الشارح وخص في البزازية : السؤال من الأصدقاء. وأشار المؤلف بقبول قول الواحد في التزكية إلى قبول قوله في الجرح وسيأتي. وليس مراد المؤلف التسوية بين الثلاثة في جميع الوجوه وإنما مراده التسوية في الاكتفاء بالواحد وبين التزكية والترجمة فرق فإن الترجمان لو كان أعمى لا يجوز عند الإمام ويجوز عند الثاني، وقدمنا أن تزكية الأعمى جائزة ولا يكون المترجم امرأة كما قدمناه عن الخزانة وتصلح للتزكية. وشرط في الظهيرية في المترجم عن الشاهد أن يكون الشاهد أعجمياً وعن الخصم أن يكون كذلك قوله : (وأطلق في الواحد فشمل العبد والمرأة والأعمى سيأتي يذكر أن المرأة والأعمى لا تجوز ترجمتهما فالظاهر أن المراد الإطلاق بالنسبة للتزكية .
His saying: 'And one person suffices for tazkiya, message, and translation, and this is according to the two (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf). Muhammad said: It is not valid except with two, because these are in the meaning of testimony. Because the judge's authority is built on the appearance of integrity, and it is through tazkiya, so number is required like in integrity. Also masculinity in the modifier is required in hudud cases. And for them (the two), it is not like testimony, for which reason the wording of testimony and the council of the judge are not required; requiring number in testimony is a stipulation of taa'abbud (devotional ruling) that does not extend beyond it. And the place of disagreement is when the opponent is not satisfied with one modifier; if the opponent accepts one, and he modifies, it is valid by consensus, as in al-Walwaljiyya. And he made absolute in tazkiya, meaning secret tazkiya. If one just upright Muslim were to say, it would be better, because integrity and Islam are required in the modifier if the testified-against is Muslim, as in al-Bazzaziyya. He made absolute regarding 'one', so it includes the slave, woman, blind, the one who was lashed for slander if he repented, the minor, one spouse for the other, parent for child and vice versa, slave for master and vice versa. Excluded from his speech is tazkiya for witness in zina, for that requires the modifier to have the capacity for testimony and the number must be four by consensus. I have not seen the ruling for tazkiya of witness for other hudud; what they said implies requiring two men for it. We restricted with secret tazkiya as precaution against public tazkiya, for public tazkiya requires all that is required in testimony: freedom, sight, etc., except the wording of testimony by consensus, because the meaning of testimony is more apparent there as it is specific to the judge's council. Likewise number is required in it according to what al-Khassaf said. He made absolute regarding 'message', so it includes the message of the judge to the modifier and the modifier to the judge, as in Fath al-Qadir, not the first as the commentator claimed. He made absolute regarding 'translation', so it includes translation from the witnesses or from the plaintiff or defendant, not the first as the commentator imagined. They said: The most precautionary in all is two. In al-Bazzaziyya: And he does not inform him that he is asking about him, and al-Sadr al-Shahid explained it because if he informs him, perhaps the modifier would deceive or intimidate him. He does not inform him that he asked about him secretly; he only seeks public tazkiya. And the judge should choose for questioning about witnesses one who is most knowledgeable of people's conditions, most mixing with people, with his integrity, knowing what is not a defect and what is a defect, not greedy nor poor so as not to be deceived by money. If there is none among his neighbors or market people that he trusts, he asks the people of his district; if he does not find a trustworthy among them, he relies on widespread reports; as the commentator mentioned. And al-Khassaf specified in al-Bazzaziyya: asking from friends. And the author indicated, by accepting the statement of one in tazkiya, that he accepts it in jarh (disqualification), and it will come. And the author did not intend equality among the three in all aspects; he merely intended equality in sufficing with one. Between tazkiya and translation there is a difference: the translator if blind is not allowed according to Imam (Abu Hanifa) but allowed according to the second (Abu Yusuf). We mentioned that tazkiya by a blind person is permissible. And the translator cannot be a woman, as we mentioned from al-Khazana, and she qualifies for tazkiya. In al-Zahiriyya, there is a condition regarding the translator: the witness must be non-Arab, and the opponent likewise. His saying: 'And he made absolute regarding one, so it includes the slave, woman, blind' – it will come that the woman and blind are not allowed as translators; so the apparent meaning is that the absolute is regarding tazkiya.
Source pages p. 112

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute on the number of persons required for tazkiya (vouching), message (conveyance), and translation (interpretation). Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf hold that one person suffices, while Muhammad requires two, analogizing these to testimony. The passage elaborates on the conditions for modifiers and translators, including that secret tazkiya accepts one modifier, but public tazkiya requires all the conditions of testimony except the wording. The judge is advised to choose trustworthy individuals for inquiry. The summary is that the author supports the position of the two (sufficiency of one) but notes that the most precautionary is two.

Key Terms
تزكية (tazkiya): Secret or public vouching for a witness's uprightness; secret tazkiya has relaxed conditions.
رسالة (risalah): Conveying a message between the judge and the modifier or vice versa.
ترجمة (tarjamah): Translation of testimony or statements from witnesses, plaintiff, or defendant.

Key Terms from Source Passage

C) One
D) None

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, one person suffices for secret tazkiya, message, and translation, following Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf, but caution recommends two.
